{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01XCdJxR11niPbcBPRto4MGR","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→//! # The Rust Prelude\n     2→//!\n     3→//! Rust comes with a variety of things in its standard library. However, if\n     4→//! you had to manually import every single thing that you used, it would be\n     5→//! very verbose. But importing a lot of things that a program never uses isn't\n     6→//! good either. A balance needs to be struck.\n     7→//!\n     8→//! The *prelude* is the list of things that Rust automatically imports into\n     9→//! every Rust program. It's kept as small as possible, and is focused on\n    10→//! things, particularly traits, which are used in almost every single Rust\n    11→//! program.\n    12→//!\n    13→//! # Other preludes\n    14→//!\n    15→//! Preludes can be seen as a pattern to make using multiple types more\n    16→//! convenient. As such, you'll find other preludes in the standard library,\n    17→//! such as [`std::io::prelude`]. Various libraries in the Rust ecosystem may\n    18→//! also define their own preludes.\n    19→//!\n    20→//! [`std::io::prelude`]: crate::io::prelude\n    21→//!\n    22→//! The difference between 'the prelude' and these other preludes is that they\n    23→//! are not automatically `use`'d, and must be imported manually. This is still\n    24→//! easier than importing all of their constituent components.\n    25→//!\n    26→//! # Prelude contents\n    27→//!\n    28→//! The items included in the prelude depend on the edition of the crate.\n    29→//! The first version of the prelude is used in Rust 2015 and Rust 2018,\n    30→//! and lives in [`std::prelude::v1`].\n    31→//! [`std::prelude::rust_2015`] and [`std::prelude::rust_2018`] re-export this prelude.\n    32→//! It re-exports the following:\n    33→//!\n    34→//! * <code>[std::marker]::{[Copy], [Send], [Sized], [Sync], [Unpin]}</code>,\n    35→//!   marker traits that indicate fundamental properties of types.\n    36→//! * <code>[std::ops]::{[Fn], [FnMut], [FnOnce]}</code>, and their analogous\n    37→//!   async traits, <code>[std::ops]::{[AsyncFn], [AsyncFnMut], [AsyncFnOnce]}</code>.\n    38→//! * <code>[std::ops]::[Drop]</code>, for implementing destructors.\n    39→//! * <code>[std::mem]::[drop]</code>, a convenience function for explicitly\n    40→//!   dropping a value.\n    41→//! * <code>[std::mem]::{[size_of], [size_of_val]}</code>, to get the size of\n    42→//!   a type or value.\n    43→//! * <code>[std::mem]::{[align_of], [align_of_val]}</code>, to get the\n    44→//!   alignment of a type or value.\n    45→//! * <code>[std::boxed]::[Box]</code>, a way to allocate values on the heap.\n    46→//! * <code>[std::borrow]::[ToOwned]</code>, the conversion trait that defines\n    47→//!   [`to_owned`], the generic method for creating an owned type from a\n    48→//!   borrowed type.\n    49→//! * <code>[std::clone]::[Clone]</code>, the ubiquitous trait that defines\n    50→//!   [`clone`][Clone::clone], the method for producing a copy of a value.\n    51→//! * <code>[std::cmp]::{[PartialEq], [PartialOrd], [Eq], [Ord]}</code>, the\n    52→//!   comparison traits, which implement the comparison operators and are often\n    53→//!   seen in trait bounds.\n    54→//! * <code>[std::convert]::{[AsRef], [AsMut], [Into], [From]}</code>, generic\n    55→//!   conversions, used by savvy API authors to create overloaded methods.\n    56→//! * <code>[std::default]::[Default]</code>, types that have default values.\n    57→//! * <code>[std::iter]::{[Iterator], [Extend], [IntoIterator], [DoubleEndedIterator], [ExactSizeIterator]}</code>,\n    58→//!   iterators of various\n    59→//!   kinds.\n    60→//! * <code>[std::option]::[Option]::{[self][Option], [Some], [None]}</code>, a\n    61→//!   type which expresses the presence or absence of a value. This type is so\n    62→//!   commonly used, its variants are also exported.\n    63→//! * <code>[std::result]::[Result]::{[self][Result], [Ok], [Err]}</code>, a type\n    64→//!   for functions that may succeed or fail. Like [`Option`], its variants are\n    65→//!   exported as well.\n    66→//! * <code>[std::string]::{[String], [ToString]}</code>, heap-allocated strings.\n    67→//! * <code>[std::vec]::[Vec]</code>, a growable, heap-allocated vector.\n    68→//!\n    69→//! The prelude used in Rust 2021, [`std::prelude::rust_2021`], includes all of the above,\n    70→//! and in addition re-exports:\n    71→//!\n    72→//! * <code>[std::convert]::{[TryFrom], [TryInto]}</code>.\n    73→//! * <code>[std::iter]::[FromIterator]</code>.\n    74→//!\n    75→//! The prelude used in Rust 2024, [`std::prelude::rust_2024`], includes all of the above,\n    76→//! and in addition re-exports:\n    77→//!\n    78→//! * <code>[std::future]::{[Future], [IntoFuture]}</code>.\n    79→//!\n    80→//! [std::borrow]: crate::borrow\n    81→//! [std::boxed]: crate::boxed\n    82→//! [std::clone]: crate::clone\n    83→//! [std::cmp]: crate::cmp\n    84→//! [std::convert]: crate::convert\n    85→//! [std::default]: crate::default\n    86→//! [std::future]: crate::future\n    87→//! [std::iter]: crate::iter\n    88→//! [std::marker]: crate::marker\n    89→//! [std::mem]: crate::mem\n    90→//! [std::ops]: crate::ops\n    91→//! [std::option]: crate::option\n    92→//! [`std::prelude::v1`]: v1\n    93→//! [`std::prelude::rust_2015`]: rust_2015\n    94→//! [`std::prelude::rust_2018`]: rust_2018\n    95→//! [`std::prelude::rust_2021`]: rust_2021\n    96→//! [`std::prelude::rust_2024`]: rust_2024\n    97→//! [std::result]: crate::result\n    98→//! [std::slice]: crate::slice\n    99→//! [std::string]: crate::string\n   100→//! [std::vec]: mod@crate::vec\n   101→//! [`to_owned`]: crate::borrow::ToOwned::to_owned\n   102→//! Rust comes with a variety of things in its standard library. However, if\n//! you had to manually import every single thing that you used, it would be\n//! very verbose. But importing a lot of things that a program never uses isn't\n//! good either. A balance needs to be struck.\n//!\n//! The *prelude* is the list of things that Rust automatically imports into\n//! every Rust program. It's kept as small as possible, and is focused on\n//! things, particularly traits, which are used in almost every single Rust\n//! program.\n//!\n//! # Other preludes\n//!\n//! Preludes can be seen as a pattern to make using multiple types more\n//! convenient. As such, you'll find other preludes in the standard library,\n//! such as [`std::io::prelude`]. Various libraries in the Rust ecosystem may\n//! also define their own preludes.\n//!\n//! [`std::io::prelude`]: crate::io::prelude\n//!\n//! The difference between 'the prelude' and these other preludes is that they\n//! are not automatically `use`'d, and must be imported manually. This is still\n//! easier than importing all of their constituent components.\n//!\n//! # Prelude contents\n//!\n//! The items included in the prelude depend on the edition of the crate.\n//! The first version of the prelude is used in Rust 2015 and Rust 2018,\n//! and lives in [`std::prelude::v1`].\n//! [`std::prelude::rust_2015`] and [`std::prelude::rust_2018`] re-export this prelude.\n//! It re-exports the following:\n//!\n//! * <code>[std::marker]::{[Copy], [Send], [Sized], [Sync], [Unpin]}</code>,\n//!   marker traits that indicate fundamental properties of types.\n//! * <code>[std::ops]::{[Fn], [FnMut], [FnOnce]}</code>, and their analogous\n//!   async traits, <code>[std::ops]::{[AsyncFn], [AsyncFnMut], [AsyncFnOnce]}</code>.\n//! * <code>[std::ops]::[Drop]</code>, for implementing destructors.\n//! * <code>[std::mem]::[drop]</code>, a convenience function for explicitly\n//!   dropping a value.\n//! * <code>[std::mem]::{[size_of], [size_of_val]}</code>, to get the size of\n//!   a type or value.\n//! * <code>[std::mem]::{[align_of], [align_of_val]}</code>, to get the\n//!   alignment of a type or value.\n//! * <code>[std::boxed]::[Box]</code>, a way to allocate values on the heap.\n//! * <code>[std::borrow]::[ToOwned]</code>, the conversion trait that defines\n//!   [`to_owned`], the generic method for creating an owned type from a\n//!   borrowed type.\n//! * <code>[std::clone]::[Clone]</code>, the ubiquitous trait that defines\n//!   [`clone`][Clone::clone], the method for producing a copy of a value.\n//! * <code>[std::cmp]::{[PartialEq], [PartialOrd], [Eq], [Ord]}</code>, the\n//!   comparison traits, which implement the comparison operators and are often\n//!   seen in trait bounds.\n//! * <code>[std::convert]::{[AsRef], [AsMut], [Into], [From]}</code>, generic\n//!   conversions, used by savvy API authors to create overloaded methods.\n//! * <code>[std::default]::[Default]</code>, types that have default values.\n//! * <code>[std::iter]::{[Iterator], [Extend], [IntoIterator], [DoubleEndedIterator], [ExactSizeIterator]}</code>,\n//!   iterators of various\n//!   kinds.\n//! * <code>[std::option]::[Option]::{[self][Option], [Some], [None]}</code>, a\n//!   type which expresses the presence or absence of a value. This type is so\n//!   commonly used, its variants are also exported.\n//! * <code>[std::result]::[Result]::{[self][Result], [Ok], [Err]}</code>, a type\n//!   for functions that may succeed or fail. Like [`Option`], its variants are\n//!   exported as well.\n//! * <code>[std::string]::{[String], [ToString]}</code>, heap-allocated strings.\n//! * <code>[std::vec]::[Vec]</code>, a growable, heap-allocated vector.\n//!\n//! The prelude used in Rust 2021, [`std::prelude::rust_2021`], includes all of the above,\n//! and in addition re-exports:\n//!\n//! * <code>[std::convert]::{[TryFrom], [TryInto]}</code>.\n//! * <code>[std::iter]::[FromIterator]</code>.\n//!\n//! The prelude used in Rust 2024, [`std::prelude::rust_2024`], includes all of the above,\n//! and in addition re-exports:\n//!\n//! * <code>[std::future]::{[Future], [IntoFuture]}</code>.\n//!\n//! [std::borrow]: crate::borrow\n//! [std::boxed]: crate::boxed\n//! [std::clone]: crate::clone\n//! [std::cmp]: crate::cmp\n//! [std::convert]: crate::convert\n//! [std::default]: crate::default\n//! [std::future]: crate::future\n//! [std::iter]: crate::iter\n//! [std::marker]: crate::marker\n//! [std::mem]: crate::mem\n//! [std::ops]: crate::ops\n//! [std::option]: crate::option\n//! [`std::prelude::v1`]: v1\n//! [`std::prelude::rust_2015`]: rust_2015\n//! [`std::prelude::rust_2018`]: rust_2018\n//! [`std::prelude::rust_2021`]: rust_2021\n//! [`std::prelude::rust_2024`]: rust_2024\n//! [std::result]: crate::result\n//! [std::slice]: crate::slice\n//! [std::string]: crate::string\n//! [std::vec]: mod@crate::vec\n//! [`to_owned`]: crate::borrow::ToOwned::to_owned\n//! [book-closures]: ../../book/ch13-01-closures.html\n//! [book-dtor]: ../../book/ch15-03-drop.html\n//! Span,\n   239→        method_name: Ident,\n   240→        self_ty: Ty<'tcx>,\n   241→        self_ty_span: Span,\n   242→        expr_id: hir::HirId,\n   243→        pick: &Pick<'tcx>,\n   244→    ) {\n   245→        // Rust 2021 and later is already using the new prelude\n   246→        if span.at_least_rust_2021() {\n   247→            return;\n   248→        }\n   249→\n   250→        // These are the fully qualified methods added to prelude in Rust 2021\n   251→        if !matches!(method_name.name, sym::try_into | sym::try_from | sym::from_iter) {\n   252→            return;\n   253→        }\n   254→\n   255→        // No need to lint if method came from std/core, as that will now be in the prelude\n   256→        if STDLIB_STABLE_CRATES.contains(&self.tcx.crate_name(pick.item.def_id.krate)) {\n   257→            return;\n   258→        }\n   259→\n   260→        // For from_iter, check if the type actually implements FromIterator.\n   261→        // If we know it does not, we don't need to warn.\n   262→        if method_name.name == sym::from_iter {\n   263→            if let Some(trait_def_id) = self.tcx.get_diagnostic_item(sym::FromIterator) {\n   264→                let any_type = self.infcx.next_ty_var(span);\n   265→                if !self\n   266→                    .infcx\n   267→                    .type_implements_trait(trait_def_id, [self_ty, any_type], self.param_env)\n   268→                    .may_apply()\n   269→                {\n   270→                    return;\n   271→                }\n   272→            }\n   273→        }\n   274→\n   275→        // No need to lint if this is an inherent method called on a specific type, like `Vec::foo(...)`,\n   276→        // since such methods take precedence over trait methods.\n   277→        if matches!(pick.kind, probe::PickKind::InherentImplPick) {\n   278→            return;\n   279→        }\n   280→\n   281→ ambiguous in Rust 2021\",\n   284→                method_name.name\n   285→            ));\n   286→\n   287→            // \"type\" refers to either a type or, more likely, a trait from which\n   288→            // the associated function or method is from.\n   289→            let container_id = pick.item.container_id(self.tcx);\n   290→            let trait_path = self.trait_path_or_bare_name(span, expr_id, container_id);\n   291→            let trait_generics = self.tcx.generics_of(container_id);\n   292→\n   293→            let trait_name =\n   294→                if trait_generics.own_params.len() <= trait_generics.has_self as usize {\n   295→                    trait_path\n   296→                } else {\n   297→                    let counts = trait_generics.own_counts();\n   298→                    format!(\n   299→                        \"{}<{}>\",\n   300→                        trait_path,\n   301→                        std::iter::repeat(\"'_\")\n   302→                            .take(counts.lifetimes)\n   303→                            .chain(std::iter::repeat(\"_\").take(\n   304→  328→                                .chain(std::iter::repeat(\"_\").take(counts.types + counts.consts))\n   329→                                .collect::<Vec<_>>()\n   330→ Applicability::MachineApplicable,\n   340→            );\n   341→        });\n   342→    }\n   343→\n   344→    fn trait_path_or_bare_name(\n   345→        &self,\n   346→        span: Span,\n   347→        expr_hir_id: HirId,\n   348→        trait_def_id: DefId,\n   349→    ) -> String {\n   350→        self.trait_path(span, expr_hir_id, trait_def_id).unwrap_or_else(|| {\n   351→            let expr_hir_id: HirId, trait_def_id: DefId) -> Option<String> {\n   357→        let applicable_traits = self.tcx.in_scope_traits(expr_hir_id)?;\n   358→        let applicable_trait = applicable_traits.iter().find(|t| t.def_id == trait_def_id)?;\n   359→        if applicable_trait.import_ids.is_empty() {\n   360→            // The trait was declared within the module, we only need 367→            .map(|&import_id| self.tcx.hir_expect_item(import_id))\n   368→            .collect();\n   369→\n   370→        // Find an identifier with which this trait was imported (note that `_` doesn't count).\n   371→        for item in import_items.iter() {\n   372→            let (_, kind) = item.expect_use();\n   373→            match kind {\n   374→                hir::UseKind::Single(ident) => {\n   375→                    if ident.name != kw::Underscore {\n   376→                        return Some(format!(\"{}\", ident.name));\n   377→                    }\n       }\n   382→        }\n   383→\n   384→        // All that is left is `_`! We need to use the full path. It doesn't matter which one we\n   385→        // pick, so just take the first one.\n   386→        match import_items[0].kind {\n   387→            ItemKind::Use(path, _) => {\n   388→                Some(join_path_idents(path.segments.iter().map(|seg| seg.ident)))\n   389→            }\n   390→            _ => {\n   391→                span_bug!(span, \"unexpected item kind, expected a use: {:?}\", import_items[0].kind);\n   392→            }\n   393→        }\n   394→    }\n   395→\n   396→    /// Creates a string version of the `expr` that includes explicit adjustments.\n   397→    /// \"disambiguate the associated function with `{}::{}(...)`\",\n                                trait_name, segment.ident,\n                            ),\n                        );\n Ty<'tcx>,\n        self_ty_span: Span,\n        expr_id: hir::HirId,\n        pick: &Pick<'tcx>,\n    ) {\n        // Rust 2021 and later is already using the new prelude\n        if span.at_least_rust_2021() {\n            return;\n        }\n\n        // These are the fully qualified methods added to prelude in Rust 2021\n        if !matches!(method_name.name, sym::try_into | sym::try_from | sym::from_iter) {\n            return;\n        }\n\n        // No need to lint if method came from std/core, as that will now be in the prelude\n        if STDLIB_STABLE_CRATES.contains(&self.tcx.crate_name(pick.item.def_id.krate)) {\n            return;\n        }\n\n        // For from_iter, check if the type actually implements FromIterator.\n        // If we know it does not, we don't need to warn.\n        if method_name.name == sym::from_iter {\n            if let Some(trait_def_id) = self.tcx.get_diagnostic_item(sym::FromIterator) {\n                let any_type = self.infcx.next_ty_var(span);\n                if !self\n                    .infcx\n                    .type_implements_trait(trait_def_id, [self_ty, any_type], self.param_env)\n                    .may_apply()\n                {\n                    return;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        // No need to lint if this is an inherent method called on a specific type, like `Vec::foo(...)`,\n        // since such methods take precedence over trait methods.\n        if matches!(pick.kind, probe::PickKind::InherentImplPick) {\n            return;\n        }\n\n        self.tcx.node_span_lint(RUST_2021_PRELUDE_COLLISIONS, expr_id, span, |lint| {\n            lint.primary_message(format!(\n                \"trait-associated function `{}` will become ambiguous in Rust 2021\",\n                method_name.name\n            ));\n\n            // \"type\" refers to either a type or, more likely, a trait from which\n            // the associated function or method is from.\n            let container_id = pick.item.container_id(self.tcx);\n            let trait_path = self.trait_path_or_bare_name(span, expr_id, container_id);\n            let trait_generics = self.tcx.generics_of(container_id);\n\n            let trait_name =\n                if trait_generics.own_params.len() <= trait_generics.has_self as usize {\n                    trait_path\n                } else {\n                    let counts = trait_generics.own_counts();\n                    format!(\n                        \"{}<{}>\",\n                        trait_path,\n                        std::iter::repeat(\"'_\")\n                            .take(counts.lifetimes)\n                            .chain(std::iter::repeat(\"_\").take(\n                                counts.types + counts.consts - trait_generics.has_self as usize\n                            ))\n                            .collect::<Vec<_>>()\n                            .join(\", \")\n                    )\n                };\n\n            let mut self_ty_name = self_ty_span\n                .find_ancestor_inside(span)\n                .and_then(|span| self.sess().source_map().span_to_snippet(span).ok())\n                .unwrap_or_else(|| self_ty.to_string());\n\n            // Get the number of generics the self type has (if an Adt) unless we can determine that\n            // the user has written the self type with generics already which we (naively) do by looking\n            // for a \"<\" in `self_ty_name`.\n            if !self_ty_name.contains('<') {\n                if let ty::Adt(def, _) = self_ty.kind() {\n                    let generics = self.tcx.generics_of(def.did());\n                    if !generics.is_own_empty() {\n                        let counts = generics.own_counts();\n                        self_ty_name += &format!(\n                            \"<{}>\",\n                            std::iter::repeat(\"'_\")\n                                .take(counts.lifetimes)\n                                .chain(std::iter::repeat(\"_\").take(counts.types + counts.consts))\n                                .collect::<Vec<_>>()\n                                .join(\", \")\n                        );\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n            lint.span_suggestion(\n                span,\n                \"disambiguate the associated function\",\n                format!(\"<{} as {}>::{}\", self_ty_name, trait_name, method_name.name,),\n                Applicability::MachineApplicable,\n            );\n        });\n    }\n\n    fn trait_path_or_bare_name(\n        &self,\n        span: Span,\n        expr_hir_id: HirId,\n        trait_def_id: DefId,\n    ) -> String {\n        self.trait_path(span, expr_hir_id, trait_def_id).unwrap_or_else(|| {\n            let key = self.tcx.def_key(trait_def_id);\n            format!(\"{}\", key.disambiguated_data.data)\n        })\n    }\n\n    fn trait_path(&self, span: Span, expr_hir_id: HirId, trait_def_id: DefId) -> Option<String> {\n        let applicable_traits = self.tcx.in_scope_traits(expr_hir_id)?;\n        let applicable_trait = applicable_traits.iter().find(|t| t.def_id == trait_def_id)?;\n        if applicable_trait.import_ids.is_empty() {\n            // The trait was declared within the module, we only need to use its name.\n            return None;\n        }\n\n        let import_items: Vec<_> = applicable_trait\n            .import_ids\n            .iter()\n            .map(|&import_id| self.tcx.hir_expect_item(import_id))\n            .collect();\n\n        // Find an identifier with which this trait was imported (note that `_` doesn't count).\n        for item in import_items.iter() {\n            let (_, kind) = item.expect_use();\n            match kind {\n                hir::UseKind::Single(ident) => {\n                    if ident.name != kw::Underscore {\n                        return Some(format!(\"{}\", ident.name));\n                    }\n                }\n                hir::UseKind::Glob => return None, // Glob import, so just use its name.\n                hir::UseKind::ListStem => unreachable!(),\n            }\n        }\n\n        // All that is left is `_`! We need to use the full path. It doesn't matter which one we\n        // pick, so just take the first one.\n        match import_items[0].kind {\n            ItemKind::Use(path, _) => {\n                Some(join_path_idents(path.segments.iter().map(|seg| seg.ident)))\n            }\n            _ => {\n                span_bug!(span, \"unexpected item kind, expected a use: {:?}\", import_items[0].kind);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Creates a string version of the `expr` that includes explicit adjustments.\n    /// Returns the string and also a bool indicating whether this is a *precise*\n    /// suggestion.\n    fn adjust_expr(\n        &self,\n        pick: &Pick<'tcx>,\n        expr: &hir::Expr<'tcx>,\n        outer: Span,\n    ) -> (String, bool) {\n        let derefs = \"*\".repeat(pick.autoderefs);\n\n        let autoref = match pick.autoref_or_ptr_adjustment {\n            Some(probe::AutorefOrPtrAdjustment::Autoref { mutbl, .. }) => mutbl.ref_prefix_str(),\n            Some(probe::AutorefOrPtrAdjustment::ToConstPtr) | None => \"\",\n            Some(probe::AutorefOrPtrAdjustment::ReborrowPin(mutbl)) => match mutbl {\n                hir::Mutability::Mut => \"Pin<&mut \",\n                hir::Mutability::Not => \"Pin<&\",\n            },\n        };\n\n        let (expr_text, precise) = if let Some(expr_text) = expr\n            .span\n            .find_ancestor_inside(outer)\n            .and_then(|span| self.sess().source_map().span_to_snippet(span).ok())\n        {\n            (expr_text, true)\n        } else {\n            (\"(..)\".to_string(), false)\n        };\n\n        let mut adjusted_text = if let Some(probe::AutorefOrPtrAdjustment::ToConstPtr) =\n            pick.autoref_or_ptr_adjustment\n        {\n            format!(\"{derefs}{expr_text} as *const _\")\n        } else {\n            format!(\"{autoref}{derefs}{expr_text}\")\n        };\n\n        if let Some(probe::AutorefOrPtrAdjustment::ReborrowPin(_)) = pick.autoref_or_ptr_adjustment\n        {\n            adjusted_text.push('>');\n        }\n\n        (adjusted_text, precise)\n    }\n}\n","numLines":442,"startLine":1,"totalLines":442}}}
